     Add "Current Show" Dashboard Block

     Context

     The dashboard (DashboardView.vue) currently has a pinned Next Show panel at
      the top of column 0 that shows the next-scheduled episode by air_date.
     There is no dashboard panel for the episode that is currently in production
      ‚ÄĒ that information only exists today inside the iPad Script Mode banner at
      the top of the dashboard, which filters /api/episodes for status === 
     'production'.

     The user wants a new draggable block called "Current Show" that:
     - Shows the in-production episode (status='production') ‚ÄĒ semantically
     matches the "Current" naming and complements (does not duplicate) Next
     Show. The user listed display fields, not selection logic; this rule
     mirrors the existing iPad-banner pattern in DashboardView.vue:334.
     - Displays: status chip, title, air date, "Edit Show" button, mini
     thumbnail.
     - Default position: directly under Next Show (i.e., first item in column
     0's draggable list ‚ÄĒ Next Show is pinned non-draggable above the draggable
     container).
     - Survives Reset Layout (added to DEFAULT_LAYOUT) and is registered as a
     normal draggable block so the user can move it.

     Approach

     1. New component: disaffected-ui/src/components/CurrentShowPanel.vue

     Modeled on NextShowPanel.vue but trimmed to the requested fields. Reuse its
      formatting helpers (formatAirDate, getStatusBgColor) by copying them
     locally (they're <30 lines combined and the existing component does not
     export them ‚ÄĒ extracting to a shared util is out of scope for this single
     sibling panel).

     Structure:
     - Header: gradient bar, mdi-broadcast icon, title "Current Show", drag
     handle class dash-drag-handle on the title row (required for the draggable
     system ‚ÄĒ see DashboardView.vue:71).
     - Body (when an in-production episode exists):
       - Mini 16x9 thumbnail (~120px wide) on the left, info on the right.
       - Status chip (colored via getStatusBgColor).
       - Episode title + episode number.
       - Air date (formatted).
       - "Edit Show" button ‚Üí /content-editor/{episode_number} (matches
     NextShowPanel line¬†88).
     - Empty state: "No episode currently in production" with subtle styling ‚ÄĒ
     do not show a CTA (the iPad banner / Next Show already cover creation
     flows).

     Data fetch (script setup):
     - GET /api/episodes with same axios setup NextShowPanel uses (it imports
     nothing special ‚ÄĒ just uses fetch/axios; check NextShowPanel's exact HTTP
     client and mirror it).
     - Filter client-side for the first episode where status === 'production'
     and !is_test_data (mirrors DashboardView.vue:332-336).
     - Then GET /api/episodes/{episode_number}/thumbnail/confirmed to get the
     poster (returns { thumbnail_url, ... } from episode.poster_16x9). If 404 /
     null, fall back to a placeholder Vuetify icon ‚ÄĒ do NOT call the full
     /thumbnails listing endpoint (heavier, scans filesystem).
     - onMounted: fetch once, then setInterval every 5 minutes (matches
     NextShowPanel cadence at line¬†222).
     - Loading skeleton + error states.

     2. Wire into DashboardView.vue

     Four edits, all in disaffected-ui/src/views/DashboardView.vue:

     1. Import (after the NextShowPanel import around line¬†192):
     import CurrentShowPanel from '@/components/CurrentShowPanel.vue'
     2. BLOCK_COLORS map (lines 199-205) ‚ÄĒ add:
     'current-show': 'orange',
     2. (Orange matches the existing "IN PRODUCTION" chip color used in
     DashboardView.vue:23.)
     3. DEFAULT_LAYOUT (lines 207-211) ‚ÄĒ prepend 'current-show' to column 0 so
     it sits directly under the pinned NextShowPanel:
     const DEFAULT_LAYOUT = [
       ['current-show', 'tools-actions'],
       ['announcements', 'preproduction'],
       ['todo', 'system-health']
     ]
     4. Template branch inside the draggable <template #item> (around lines
     81-169) ‚ÄĒ add at the top of the v-if/v-else-if chain so it renders first:
     <CurrentShowPanel v-if="element === 'current-show'" />
     <v-card v-else-if="element === 'tools-actions'" ...>
     4. (Convert the existing v-if="element === 'tools-actions'" to v-else-if.)
     5. LAYOUT_KEY bump (line¬†214): bump from 'dashboard-layout-v2' to
     'dashboard-layout-v3'. loadLayout() already merges newly-registered blocks
     into column 0 for users with saved layouts (lines 221-242), but bumping the
      key is the cleanest way to guarantee the new block appears in the intended
      spot rather than appended to wherever the merge logic puts it. (The
     previous bump from v1‚Üív2 in this file followed the same pattern.)

     3. No backend changes required

     /api/episodes already returns status and all needed fields.
     /api/episodes/{n}/thumbnail/confirmed already exists at
     app/routers/episodes/thumbnails_router.py:270. Status value 'production' is
      already in active use.

     Critical files

     - NEW: disaffected-ui/src/components/CurrentShowPanel.vue
     - MODIFY: disaffected-ui/src/views/DashboardView.vue (5 edits above)

     Reused utilities / patterns

     - Drag-handle wiring pattern: DashboardView.vue:71
     (handle=".dash-drag-handle").
     - Status‚Üícolor map and formatAirDate helper: copy from
     NextShowPanel.vue:173-218.
     - "Edit Show" button route shape: NextShowPanel.vue:88
     (/content-editor/{episode_number}).
     - Production-episode filter logic: DashboardView.vue:332-336.
     - Confirmed thumbnail endpoint:
     app/routers/episodes/thumbnails_router.py:270 (GET 
     /api/episodes/{n}/thumbnail/confirmed).
     - Block color/layout registration pattern: DashboardView.vue:199-214.

     Verification

     1. Static checks (mandatory per CLAUDE.md):
     cd /srv/show-build/disaffected-ui && npm run lint -- --fix
     1. No backend changes, so no docker compose restart server needed.
     2. Manual UI test at https://192.168.51.207:8091:
       - Hard-reload dashboard (the LAYOUT_KEY bump should give every user a
     fresh default layout containing the new block).
       - Confirm Current Show appears directly below Next Show in column¬†0.
       - If an episode with status='production' exists: status chip, title,
     airdate, mini thumbnail (or fallback icon), and "Edit Show" button all
     render. Button navigates to /content-editor/{number}.
       - If no production episode: empty state shows.
       - Drag the Current Show block to another column, refresh ‚ÄĒ position
     persists in localStorage['dashboard-layout-v3'].
       - Click "Reset Layout" ‚ÄĒ block returns to top of column 0, under Next
     Show.
       - Wait/observe ‚Č•5 min OR temporarily lower the interval and confirm
     auto-refresh fires (network tab shows repeated /api/episodes calls).
     3. Edge case to eyeball: when the in-production episode has no confirmed
     poster (poster_16x9 is null), confirm the fallback icon renders rather than
      a broken image.

‚ĚĮ In the content editor, there is a thumbnail for there's an image location set 
   up for a thumbnail, and it detects existence of a thumbnail based on file    
  names. Is that right?                                                         

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Yes, that's correct ‚ÄĒ and there are actually two layers to it:

  1. Discovery (filename-based) ‚ÄĒ GET /api/episodes/{n}/thumbnails at
  app/routers/episodes/thumbnails_router.py:18
  - Scans two locations:
    - {episode_dir}/thumbnails/ (plus one level of subdirs)
    - {episode_dir}/exports/ (legacy)
  - Matches files whose name starts with poster and has a .jpg/.jpeg/.png/.webp
  extension (case-insensitive).
  - Files with 16x9 in the name get confidence: "high" ‚ÄĒ ranked first.
  Everything else is "normal".
  - Sorts by confidence then modification time (newest first).

  2. Confirmed/protected pick (database-backed) ‚ÄĒ GET 
  /api/episodes/{n}/thumbnail/confirmed at
  app/routers/episodes/thumbnails_router.py:270
  - Reads episode.poster_16x9 from the DB ‚ÄĒ the URL of the thumbnail the user
  explicitly "took" via the editor's thumbnail picker.
  - Filename detection finds candidates; the user picks one and that selection
  is persisted in the database column.

  So the flow is: filenames make a thumbnail discoverable; the DB column records
   which discovered file is the official one. CLAUDE.md also notes that non-PNG
  candidates are auto-converted to PNG via a Celery task on the assets queue.

  The CurrentShowPanel I just added uses the confirmed endpoint (#2) ‚ÄĒ so it
  only shows a thumbnail once you've taken/confirmed one in the editor. If you'd
   rather have it fall back to the highest-confidence discovered file when
  nothing is confirmed, that's a small change.

‚ÄĽ recap: Goal: add a "Current Show" dashboard block under "Next Show" pulling the in-production episode. Block is built, wired into DashboardView, and lint passes. Next: hard-reload https://192.168.51.207:8091 to verify it renders. (disable recaps in /config)

  Why those items will never get descriptions on their own:
  1. The segment sweep (auto_description_service.py:705-723) only generates for
  segment | interview | coldopen ‚ÄĒ close items are not eligible, so any close
  listed in the gate's item_types will block forever unless someone writes the

  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ How should we unblock episode-description generation? ‚Üí Gate: ignore

‚ĚĮ explaion to me in more simple terms why there is the deadlock                 

‚óŹ Sure ‚ÄĒ here's the plain-English version:

  The rule: "Don't generate the show description until every segment, interview,
   and close item has its own description filled in."

  The problem: Some items in the rundown are empty placeholders ‚ÄĒ like the
  "Close" item that's just a stub, or "Segment-5" with no script written in it
  yet. They're sitting there on the rundown, but they have no actual content.

  The deadlock: The system is waiting for those empty items to get descriptions.
   But:

  - The auto-describer refuses to write descriptions for empty items (it needs
  at least 100 characters of script to work with).
  - The auto-describer also won't touch "Close" items at all ‚ÄĒ it only writes
  descriptions for segments, interviews, and cold opens. Closes are excluded by
  design.

  So you have two items that:
  - Block the show description from generating, but
  - Can never get a description themselves (one because it's empty, one because
  the system isn't allowed to describe it).

  It's like waiting for two people to RSVP before you can send out the party
  invitations ‚ÄĒ except those two people don't have phones, and one of them isn't
   even on the guest list.

  That's it. Show description sits empty forever, every 2 minutes the sweep
  checks, sees the same two empty placeholders, and gives up.

‚ĚĮ lets modify and add to the decision logic.                                    
                                                                                
  1. If an episode has items of the required types, but one or more of the      
  segments is <100 chars, build a description hased on all of the availible     
  content.                                                                      
                                                                                
  2. Allow the auto describer to touch the close items but unless requested     
  dont use the close content in the show description                            

‚óŹ I'll make three surgical changes to auto_description_service.py and restart
  the server.

‚óŹ Here's what's happening right now: the worker is in an infinite loop. Each
  tick picks ep 270, hits the 540-second Celery soft time limit waiting on
  Ollama to generate with qwen2.5:latest, then the next sweep tick picks ep 270
  again. Forever.

  Why Ollama is slow:
  - Ollama (192.168.51.197) currently has only llama3:latest loaded in VRAM (the
   others are offline).
  - episode_description is configured to use qwen2.5:latest, which has to be
  loaded from disk on every call. That cold-load + 600-token generation on a
  busy/shared box is exceeding the 9-minute Celery soft limit.
  - Segment descriptions use the same model, but they were likely generated
  earlier when the model was warm ‚ÄĒ and the task time limit per segment is the
  same, but the prompt is much smaller (a single segment vs. all 4 segments
  concatenated).

  There's also a secondary bug: episode-desc has no retry-attempt counter, so
  any episode that hits a timeout will be picked on the very next sweep tick, in
   perpetuity. The segment sweep has auto_generate_attempts < 5 to break loops;
  the episode sweep has nothing.

  End-to-end working. Summary of what we did this session for the
  LLM-description path:

  1. Three logic changes in app/services/auto_description_service.py: gate
  ignores items with <100 chars of script, segment sweep now eligible for close
  items, episode-description prompt excludes close content unless opted in via
  the new include_close_in_description setting.
  2. Switched models in api_configs: episode_description.model and
  episode_short_description.model ‚Üí llama3:latest. The previous values
  (qwen2.5:latest and the global qwen3:32b-q4_K_M fallback) were not loaded in
  Ollama VRAM and the cold-load was busting Celery's 540s soft time limit.
  3. Restarted server, beat, and worker to pick up the code and config changes;
  also manually re-enqueued ep 270's short after a worker restart killed it
  mid-flight.

  Two follow-ups worth noting (not implemented ‚ÄĒ flag if you want to address):
  - Ep-short orphan risk: the sweep only fires
  generate_episode_short_description as a follow-up to
  generate_episode_description. If a worker restarts between the two calls, the
  short is lost forever. A small standalone "shorts sweep" or moving the short
  call into the next sweep tick would prevent that.
  - No retry-attempt counter on episode-desc: a permanently failing episode will
   be picked on every 2-min tick forever (we saw this with the qwen2.5 timeout).
   The segment sweep has auto_generate_attempts < 5; the episode sweep has
  nothing comparable.

      382 +function getStatusColor(status) {

‚óŹ Lint clean. Summary of the restyle:

  Look & feel
  - Soft #fafafa modal body with white <section> cards, subtle borders, small
  uppercase section headers (Identity / Description / Schedule & Status / People
   / Identifiers).
  - Tabs slimmed to 36 px tall, 0.75rem text.
  - Sectioned layout gives more breathing room between groups while keeping
  fields tight.

  Field compaction
  - All fields use Vuetify density="compact" plus compact-field overrides: 32 px
   input height, 0.82‚Äď0.85rem font, 0.75rem labels.
  - dense v-row for tight horizontal grids.

  Description
  - auto-grow + rows="6" baseline + min-height: 140px so even an empty box looks
   substantial; with auto-grow it expands to fit all text without internal
  scrolling.
  - Generation-by-model hint moved to the section header (purple/italic) so it
  doesn't crowd the input.

  Read-only fields
  - Episode #, Total Duration, Episode Asset ID rendered with a readonly-field
  class: light grey background, dimmed text, disabled attribute so the cursor is
   also "not allowed". Visually clearly non-editable.

  Production status colorization
  - Imports getColorValue + resolveVuetifyColor from @/utils/themeColorMap (same
   helpers ShowInfoHeader uses).
  - Selection slot renders the status as a colored v-chip (uppercase, tonal
  flat) tinted with the status color.
  - Dropdown items also render as colored chips so all four options are
  color-coded at a glance.
  - Outline of the v-select itself takes the same status tint via a CSS custom
  property.

  Test in the browser by opening any episode and clicking Edit Episode Details
  next to the title ‚ÄĒ Basic Info should feel noticeably tighter per-field but
  more spacious overall, the description should auto-grow to show everything,
  and the Production Status field should pulse its color through the chip and
  outline.

      398  
      399 +// Normalize incoming airDate/airTime so the native HTML date/
          +time inputs                                                   
      400 +// can render them. The parent may pass a full ISO datetime, a
          + date-only                                                    
      401 +// string, or empty.                                          
      402 +const airDateInput = computed(() => {                         
      403 +  const v = props.airDate                                     
      404 +  if (!v) return ''                                           
      405 +  // Already YYYY-MM-DD                                       
      406 +  if (/^\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2}$/.test(v)) return v                 
      407 +  // ISO datetime ‚ÄĒ strip after the 'T' or ' '                
      408 +  const m = String(v).match(/^(\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2})/)           
      409 +  return m ? m[1] : ''                                        
      410 +})                                                            
      411 +                                                              
      412 +const airTimeInput = computed(() => {                         
      413 +  const v = props.airTime                                     
      414 +  if (!v) return ''                                           
      415 +  // Strip seconds if present (HH:MM:SS -> HH:MM)             
      416 +  const m = String(v).match(/^(\d{2}:\d{2})/)                 
      417 +  return m ? m[1] : ''                                        
      418 +})                                                            
      419 +                                                              
      420  function getStatusColor(status) {
      421    if (!status) return 'grey'
      422    try {

‚óŹ All four addressed:

  1. All fields now have persistent-placeholder ‚ÄĒ the floating label always
  shows above the box (Subtitle won't disappear when empty).
  2. Air date / time bind to airDateInput / airTimeInput computeds that
  normalize whatever the parent sends (full ISO datetime, date-only, or
  HH:MM:SS) into the YYYY-MM-DD / HH:MM formats the native HTML inputs require.
  Edits emit unchanged back to the parent.
  3. Timezone options switched to abbreviations: ET / CT / MT / PT / UTC.
  4. Production Status ‚ÄĒ the selection slot now renders a full-bleed <div 
  class="status-chip-fill"> instead of a small chip. CSS strips the v-select's
  inner padding (v-field__field, v-field__input ‚Üí padding:¬†0) so the colored
  block extends edge-to-edge ‚ÄĒ no inset gap, the entire dropdown is one solid
  colored button. Dropdown items also render as full-bleed colored bars.

  If air date/time still load empty after this, the parent prop is genuinely
  empty for that episode ‚ÄĒ let me know and I'll trace upstream from
  ShowInfoHeader ‚Üí ContentEditor.

‚óŹ All three tasks done ‚ÄĒ lint clean. Summary of what shipped:

  Bug fix ‚ÄĒ slug/subtitle write paths

  ContentEditor.vue:7522-7577 ‚ÄĒ handleSlugChange and handleSubtitleChange were
  writing into this.currentRundownItem (the currently-selected segment). Both
  now write to currentEpisodeSlug / currentEpisodeSubtitle (episode-level),
  matching the pattern used by guest/title/description.

  Also extended the generic update-episode-field fieldMap
  (ContentEditor.vue:4268) to include title, slug, and guest, so any future
  component can route through one channel.

  Other read-paths I audited (all OK):

  - title ‚Üź currentEpisodeTitle ‚úÖ
  - guest ‚Üź currentEpisodeGuest ‚úÖ
  - description ‚Üź currentEpisodeDescription ‚úÖ
  - airDate/airTime/airTimezone ‚Üź currentAirDate/Time/Timezone ‚úÖ
  - productionStatus ‚Üź currentProductionStatus ‚úÖ
  - episodeNumber ‚Üź currentEpisodeNumber ‚úÖ
  - episodeAssetId ‚Üź currentEpisodeAssetId (computed; falls back to first
  rundown item's assetID ‚ÄĒ episode-level by design)
  - duration ‚Üź duration (computed elsewhere, episode-wide)

  Layout swap (Basic Info)

  - Top right: Schedule & Status (was Identity) ‚ÄĒ Air Date, Air Time, Timezone,
  Production Status stacked vertically since the column is narrow.
  - Body left col: Identity (was Schedule & Status) ‚ÄĒ Episode #, Asset ID, Total
   Duration (all read-only) + People (Guest).
  - Body right col: Description (unchanged).
  - Removed the standalone "Identifiers & Computed" section since its fields
  moved into Identity.

  Meta tab populated

  Four sections, all wired through the existing update-episode-field channel:
  - Classification ‚ÄĒ Tags (text), Explicit (checkbox), Content Warnings
  (textarea)
  - Publishing ‚ÄĒ Publish Status, Visibility (selects)
  - Credits ‚ÄĒ Producer, Editor, Recording Date
  - Internal Notes ‚ÄĒ multi-line notes field

  Distribution-specific fields (Omny / YouTube / Twitter / Instagram / Facebook
  / TikTok) intentionally left out of Meta ‚ÄĒ those belong in the Distribution
  tab when we get to it.

‚ĚĮ How difficult is it to add a new status? To the production statuses and make  
  sure that those appear everywhere that the production status is displayed or  
  selectable or modifiable, including everything everything down to the color   
  selector.                                                                     

‚óŹ Let me audit where statuses live so I can give you a real answer.

  Searched for 6 patterns, read 1 file, listed 1 directory (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Honest assessment after auditing the codebase:

  Current difficulty: Moderate. The status list is duplicated across ~9 places.
  Adding one new status today touches:

  Frontend (~7 edits):
  1. composables/useEpisodeMetadata.js:63 ‚ÄĒ the composable default (closest
  thing to canonical)
  2. composables/useEditorUtils.js:186 ‚ÄĒ duplicate array
  3. components/content-editor/ShowInfoHeader.vue:455 ‚ÄĒ prop default
  4. components/content-editor/modals/EpisodeDetailsModal.vue:464 ‚ÄĒ prop default
   + the hardcoded fallback color map in getStatusColor
  5. components/content-editor/MetadataPanel.vue:761 ‚ÄĒ statusOptions ref
  6. components/content-editor/EditorPanel.vue:1946 ‚ÄĒ statusOptions computed
  7. views/EpisodesView.vue:919 ‚ÄĒ filter dropdown options
  8. components/NextShowPanel.vue:210-217 ‚ÄĒ hardcoded getStatusBgColor map

  ColorSelector (good news): ColorSelector.vue:669 is already declared with 5
  statuses (Draft, Approved, Production, Promotion, Completed) ‚ÄĒ it's actually
  ahead of the rest of the codebase. So adding a status to ColorSelector means
  appending one entry to that array; the picker UI handles the rest, and
  themeColorMap.getColorValue('your-status') will then return whatever color the
   user picks (DB-backed via /api/settings/colors).

  Backend (~1-2 edits, only if relevant):
  - app/services/auto_description_service.py:712 and :1123 hardcode WHERE 
  e.status IN ('draft', 'production') for the auto-description sweeps. If the
  new status should also trigger auto-generation, add it here. Otherwise no-op.
  - Episode model column is String(50) ‚ÄĒ no enum constraint, no migration
  needed.

  The fragility: If you add a status to (1) but forget (2)‚Äď(8), it shows up in
  some dropdowns but not others, and the color falls back to grey in the
  components with hardcoded maps.

  Recommended one-time refactor (~1 hour) to make future status additions 
  trivial:

  Create a single source of truth ‚ÄĒ e.g., src/utils/productionStatuses.js:
  export const PRODUCTION_STATUSES = [
    { value: 'draft', title: 'Draft' },
    { value: 'approved', title: 'Approved' },
    { value: 'production', title: 'Production' },
    { value: 'promotion', title: 'Promotion' },
    { value: 'completed', title: 'Completed' },
  ]
  Import it in all 7 frontend spots and delete the local arrays. Replace the 2
  hardcoded color maps (NextShowPanel, EpisodeDetailsModal fallback) with calls
  to getColorValue(status) so they pick up the database colors automatically.
  After this refactor, adding a new status = editing one file + picking a color 
  in the ColorSelector UI.

  Want me to do the refactor now? It's contained, low-risk, and would make this
  question vanish forever.

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ three changes to MetadataPanel.vue:

  1. Segment Info is now its own always-expanded block. Pulled out of the
  draggable expansion-panels system, rendered above the collapsible zone, with a
   slim header bar (mdi-information-outline + "Segment Info") and an always-open
   body. Removed 'segmentinfo' from panelOrder so it doesn't double-render in
  the draggable area below.
  2. Priority field removed from the UI. The chips, combobox, label ‚ÄĒ all gone
  from the template. The DB column is untouched, and the JS (priorityInput,
  parsedPriorities, priorityOptions, getPriorityColor, handlePriorityInput,
  commitPriorityInput, removePriority) is left in place with // 
  eslint-disable-line no-unused-vars so it stays dormant and easy to re-enable
  later.
  3. Duration moved inline with the ID. Standalone duration field is gone;
  instead a small mdi-timer-outline + duration string sits flush-right on the
  same row as the ID at the top of Segment Info. Read-only display only (matches
   the previous behavior ‚ÄĒ the old field was readonly too).

  Test by selecting any rundown item in the editor ‚ÄĒ the right sidebar should
  show the new always-visible Segment Info block at the top with ID and duration
   on one row, and the rest (Asset Pool, People, Speaker, Versions, AssetGen)
  still draggable/collapsible below.

‚óŹ Lint clean. Summary:

  Color storage ‚ÄĒ no DB schema change needed. Colors live as a JSON object in
  the Settings table under theme_colors_default (via settings_colors_router).
  Adding new keys is just adding properties to that JSON, which the existing
  endpoints already accept. The default 'block-header': 'blue' lives in
  themeColorMap.js as a fallback so the new color renders immediately even
  before anyone touches the Settings UI.

  What was added:

  1. themeColorMap.js ‚ÄĒ added 'block-header': 'blue' default so
  getColorValue('block-header') returns 'blue' until customized. Also fixed
  legacy 'scheduled' and 'running' defaults while I was there.
  2. ColorSelector.vue ‚ÄĒ new generalUiTypes = ref(['Block-Header']) ref,
  registered with the -ui suffix in both load paths and the save path. Added a
  "General UI" section table at the bottom of the picker (mirrors the Global
  Action Colors layout). New formatGeneralUiName helper. When the user picks a
  color and clicks Save, it writes both block-header-ui (the picker's internal
  key) and block-header (the consumer-facing key) into the JSON profile.
  3. MetadataPanel.vue ‚ÄĒ Segment Info block header now has
  :style="blockHeaderStyle", a computed that resolves
  getColorValue('block-header') ‚Üí Vuetify color hex. The static CSS uses #1976D2
   blue as the baked-in fallback; the inline style takes over once a color
  exists in the DB or default map.

  To verify in the browser:
  1. Open Settings ‚Üí Interface ‚Üí Color Selector ‚Üí scroll to the new "General UI"
   section.
  2. The "Block Header" row will be there with a default Blue.
  3. Open the content editor and select a rundown item ‚ÄĒ the Segment Info header
   at the top of the right sidebar should now be blue with white text.
  4. Change the color in Color Selector, save, refresh the editor ‚ÄĒ the header
  color should follow.

  Future: when you want another configurable UI color (e.g. sidebar background,
  save-button color, panel divider), just append the name to generalUiTypes and
  reference it via getColorValue('your-key') in CSS or computed style. No
  backend or settings infra changes needed.
